<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schweiz_Genf_IRK-Museum.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Schweiz_Genf_IRK-Museum.jpg/220px-Schweiz_Genf_IRK-Museum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Schweiz_Genf_IRK-Museum.jpg/330px-Schweiz_Genf_IRK-Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Schweiz_Genf_IRK-Museum.jpg/440px-Schweiz_Genf_IRK-Museum.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schweiz_Genf_IRK-Museum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entry to the International Red Cross and Red Crescent Museum in Geneva</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_Turkish_Red_Crescent_Staff.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4032" data-file-width="3024" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/A_Turkish_Red_Crescent_Staff.jpg/220px-A_Turkish_Red_Crescent_Staff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/A_Turkish_Red_Crescent_Staff.jpg/330px-A_Turkish_Red_Crescent_Staff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/A_Turkish_Red_Crescent_Staff.jpg/440px-A_Turkish_Red_Crescent_Staff.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_Turkish_Red_Crescent_Staff.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Red_Crescent" title="Turkish Red Crescent">Turkish Red Crescent</a> staff conducting activities for children</div></div></div>
<p>Altogether, there are about 97 million people worldwide who serve with the ICRC, the International Federation, and the National Societies, the majority with the latter.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The 1965 International Conference in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> adopted seven basic principles which should be shared by all parts of the Movement, and they were added to the official statutes of the Movement in 1986.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fundamental_principles">Fundamental principles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Fundamental principles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the 20th International Conference in Neue Hofburg, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, from 2–9 October 1965, delegates "proclaimed" seven fundamental principles which are shared by all components of the Movement, and they were added to the official statutes of the Movement in 1986. The durability and universal acceptance is a result of the process through which they came into being in the form they have. Rather than an effort to arrive at agreement, it was an attempt to discover what successful operations and organisational units, over the past 100 years, had in common. As a result, the Fundamental Principles of the Red Cross and Red Crescent were not revealed, but <i>found –</i> through a deliberate and participative process of discovery.
</p><p>That makes it even more important to note that the text that appears under each "heading" is an integral part of the Principle in question and not an interpretation that can vary with time and place.
</p><p><b>Humanity</b>
</p><p>The International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement, born of a desire to bring assistance without discrimination to the wounded on the battlefield, endeavours, in its international and national capacity, to prevent and alleviate human suffering wherever it may be found. Its purpose is to protect life and health and to ensure respect for the human being. It promotes mutual understanding, friendship, cooperation and lasting peace amongst all peoples.
</p><p><b>Impartiality</b>
</p><p>It makes no discrimination as to nationality, race, religious beliefs, class or political opinions. It endeavours to relieve the suffering of individuals, being guided solely by their needs, and to give priority to the most urgent cases of distress.
</p><p><b>Neutrality</b>
</p><p>In order to continue to enjoy the confidence of all, the Movement may not take sides in hostilities or engage at any time in controversies of a political, racial, religious or ideological nature.
</p><p><b>Independence</b>
</p><p>The Movement is independent. The National Societies, while auxiliaries in the humanitarian services of their governments and subject to the laws of their respective countries, must always maintain their autonomy so that they may be able at all times to act in accordance with the principles of the Movement.
</p><p><b>Voluntary Service</b>
</p><p>It is a voluntary relief movement not prompted in any manner by desire for gain.
</p><p><b>Unity</b>
</p><p>There can be only one Red Cross or one Red Crescent Society in any one country. It must be open to all. It must carry on its humanitarian work throughout its territory.
</p><p><b>Universality</b>
</p><p>The International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement, in which all Societies have equal status and share equal responsibilities and duties in helping each other, is worldwide.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Conference_and_the_Standing_Commission">International Conference and the Standing Commission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: International Conference and the Standing Commission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span class="anchor" id="International_Conference"></span><span class="anchor" id="Standing_Commission"></span>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Standing_Commission_of_the_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent" title="Standing Commission of the Red Cross and Red Crescent">Standing Commission of the Red Cross and Red Crescent</a></div>
<p>The International Conference of the Red Cross and Red Crescent, which occurs once every four years, is the highest institutional body of the Movement. It gathers delegations from all of the national societies as well as from the ICRC, the IFRC and the signatory states to the Geneva Conventions. In between the conferences, the <a href="/wiki/Standing_Commission_of_the_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent" title="Standing Commission of the Red Cross and Red Crescent">Standing Commission of the Red Cross and Red Crescent</a> acts as the supreme body and supervises implementation of and compliance with the resolutions of the conference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> In addition, the Standing Commission coordinates the cooperation between the ICRC and the IFRC. It consists of two representatives from the ICRC (including its president), two from the IFRC (including its president), and five individuals who are elected by the International Conference. The Standing Commission convenes every six months on average. Moreover, a convention of the Council of Delegates of the Movement takes place every two years in the course of the conferences of the General Assembly of the International Federation. The Council of Delegates plans and coordinates joint activities for the Movement.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: International Committee of the Red Cross">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mission">Mission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Mission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_ICRC.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="231" data-file-width="200" decoding="async" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Flag_of_the_ICRC.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_ICRC.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Flag_of_the_ICRC.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_ICRC.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Flag_of_the_ICRC.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_ICRC.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_ICRC.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The emblem of the International Committee of the Red Cross (French: Comité international de la Croix-rouge)</div></div></div>
<p>The official mission of the ICRC as an impartial, neutral, and independent organization is to stand for the protection of the life and dignity of victims of international and internal armed conflicts. According to the 1997 Seville Agreement, it is the "Lead Agency" of the Movement in conflicts.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Responsibilities">Responsibilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Responsibilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The core tasks of the committee, which are derived from the Geneva Conventions and its own statutes, are the following:
</p>
<ul><li>to monitor compliance of warring parties with the Geneva Conventions</li>
<li>to organize nursing and care for those who are wounded on the battlefield</li>
<li>to supervise the treatment of prisoners of war</li>
<li>to help with the search for missing persons in an armed conflict (<a href="/wiki/Restoring_Family_Links" title="Restoring Family Links">tracing service</a>)</li>
<li>to organize protection and care for civil populations</li>
<li>to arbitrate between warring parties in an armed conflict</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status_and_organization">Legal status and organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Legal status and organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The ICRC is headquartered in the Swiss city of Geneva and has external offices in about 80 countries. It has about 12,000 staff members worldwide, about 800 of them working in its Geneva headquarters, 1,200 expatriates with about half of them serving as delegates managing its international missions and the other half being specialists like doctors, agronomists, engineers or interpreters, and about 10,000 members of individual national societies working on site.
</p><p>According to Swiss law, the ICRC is defined as a private association. Contrary to popular belief, the ICRC is not a <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">non-governmental organization</a> in the most common sense of the term, nor is it an international organization. As it limits its members (a process called cooptation) to Swiss nationals only, it does not have a policy of open and unrestricted membership for individuals like other legally defined NGOs. The word "international" in its name does not refer to its membership but to the worldwide scope of its activities as defined by the Geneva Conventions. The ICRC has special privileges and legal immunities in many countries, based on national law in these countries or through agreements between the committee and respective national governments.
</p><p>According to its statutes, it consists of 15 to 25 Swiss-citizen members, which it coopts for a period of four years. There is no limit to the number of terms an individual member can have although a three-quarters majority of all members is required for re-election after the third term.
</p><p>The leading organs of the ICRC are the Directorate and the Assembly. The Directorate is the executive body of the committee. It consists of a general director and five directors in the areas of "Operations", "Human Resources", "Resources and Operational Support", "Communication", and "International Law and Cooperation within the Movement". The members of the Directorate are appointed by the Assembly to serve for four years. The Assembly, consisting of all of the members of the committee, convenes on a regular basis and is responsible for defining aims, guidelines, and strategies and for supervising the financial matters of the committee. The president of the Assembly is also the president of the committee as a whole. Furthermore, the Assembly elects a five-member Assembly Council which has the authority to decide on behalf of the full Assembly in some matters. The council is also responsible for organizing the Assembly meetings and for facilitating communication between the Assembly and the Directorate.
</p><p>Due to Geneva's location in the French-speaking part of Switzerland, the ICRC usually acts under its French name <i>Comité international de la Croix-Rouge</i> (CICR). The official symbol of the ICRC is the Red Cross on white background with the words "COMITE INTERNATIONAL GENEVE" circling the cross.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Funding_and_financial_matters">Funding and financial matters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Funding and financial matters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The 2009 budget of the ICRC amounts to more than 1 billion Swiss francs. Most of that money comes from the States, including Switzerland in its capacity as the depositary state of the Geneva Conventions, from national Red Cross societies, the signatory states of the Geneva Conventions, and from international organizations like the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. All payments to the ICRC are voluntary and are received as donations based on two types of appeals issued by the committee: an annual <i>Headquarters Appeal</i> to cover its internal costs and <i>Emergency Appeals</i> for its individual missions.
</p><p>The ICRC asked donors for more than 1.1 billion Swiss francs to fund its work in 2010. Afghanistan was projected to become the ICRC's biggest humanitarian operation (at 86 million Swiss francs, an 18% increase over the initial 2009 budget), followed by Iraq (85 million francs) and Sudan (76 million francs). The initial 2010 field budget for medical activities of 132 million francs represented an increase of 12 million francs over 2009.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="IFRC_2">IFRC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: IFRC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Societies" title="International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies">International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities_and_organization">Activities and organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Activities and organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_and_responsibilities">Mission and responsibilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Mission and responsibilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IFRC_logo_2020.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="369" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/IFRC_logo_2020.svg/220px-IFRC_logo_2020.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/IFRC_logo_2020.svg/330px-IFRC_logo_2020.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/IFRC_logo_2020.svg/440px-IFRC_logo_2020.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IFRC_logo_2020.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Emblem of the IFRC</div></div></div>
<p>The International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies coordinates cooperation between national Red Cross and Red Crescent societies throughout the world and supports the foundation of new national societies in countries where no official society exists. On the international stage, the IFRC organizes and leads relief assistance missions after emergencies such as natural disasters, manmade disasters, epidemics, mass refugee flights, and other emergencies. As per the 1997 Seville Agreement, the IFRC is the Lead Agency of the Movement in any emergency situation which does not take place as part of an armed conflict. The IFRC cooperates with the national societies of those countries affected – each called the <i>Operating National Society</i> (ONS) – as well as the national societies of other countries willing to offer assistance – called <i>Participating National Societies</i> (PNS). Among the 187 national societies admitted to the General Assembly of the International Federation as full members or observers, about 25–30 regularly work as PNS in other countries. The most active of those are the <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">American Red Cross</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Red_Cross" title="British Red Cross">British Red Cross</a>, the <a href="/wiki/German_Red_Cross" title="German Red Cross">German Red Cross</a>, and the Red Cross societies of <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Red_Cross" title="Swedish Red Cross">Sweden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Red_Cross" title="Norwegian Red Cross">Norway</a>. Another major mission of the IFRC which has gained attention in recent years is its commitment to work towards a codified, worldwide ban on the use of <a href="/wiki/Land_mine" title="Land mine">land mines</a> and to bring medical, psychological, and social support for people injured by land mines.
</p><p>The tasks of the IFRC can therefore be summarized as follows:
</p>
<ul><li>to promote humanitarian principles and values</li>
<li>to provide relief assistance in emergency situations of large magnitude, such as natural disasters</li>
<li>to support the national societies with disaster preparedness through the education of voluntary members and the provision of equipment and relief supplies</li>
<li>to support local health care projects</li>
<li>to support the national societies with youth-related activities</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status_and_organization_2">Legal status and organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Legal status and organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ambulance_of_the_Italian_Red_Cross_in_Parma,_2019.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2970" data-file-width="3960" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Ambulance_of_the_Italian_Red_Cross_in_Parma%2C_2019.jpg/220px-Ambulance_of_the_Italian_Red_Cross_in_Parma%2C_2019.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Ambulance_of_the_Italian_Red_Cross_in_Parma%2C_2019.jpg/330px-Ambulance_of_the_Italian_Red_Cross_in_Parma%2C_2019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Ambulance_of_the_Italian_Red_Cross_in_Parma%2C_2019.jpg/440px-Ambulance_of_the_Italian_Red_Cross_in_Parma%2C_2019.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ambulance_of_the_Italian_Red_Cross_in_Parma,_2019.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ambulance of the Italian Red Cross</div></div></div>
<p>The IFRC has its headquarters in Geneva. It also runs five zone offices (Africa, Americas, Asia Pacific, Europe, Middle East-North Africa), 14 permanent regional offices and has about 350 delegates in more than 60 delegations around the world. The legal basis for the work of the IFRC is its constitution. The executive body of the IFRC is a secretariat, led by a secretary general. The secretariat is supported by five divisions including "Programme Services", "Humanitarian values and humanitarian diplomacy", "National Society and Knowledge Development" and "Governance and Management Services".
</p><p>The highest decision-making body of the IFRC is its General Assembly, which convenes every two years with delegates from all of the national societies. Among other tasks, the General Assembly elects the secretary general. Between the convening of General Assemblies, the Governing Board is the leading body of the IFRC. It has the authority to make decisions for the IFRC in a number of areas. The Governing Board consists of the president and the vice presidents of the IFRC, the chairpersons of the Finance and Youth Commissions, and twenty elected representatives from national societies.
</p><p>The symbol of the IFRC is the combination of the Red Cross (left) and Red Crescent (right) on a white background surrounded by a red rectangular frame.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Funding_and_financial_matters_2">Funding and financial matters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Funding and financial matters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The main parts of the budget of the IFRC are funded by contributions from the national societies which are members of the IFRC and through revenues from its investments. The exact amount of contributions from each member society is established by the Finance Commission and approved by the General Assembly. Any additional funding, especially for unforeseen expenses for relief assistance missions, is raised by "appeals"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> published by the IFRC and comes for voluntary donations by national societies, governments, other organizations, corporations, and individuals.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Societies">National Societies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: National Societies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_recognition">Official recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Official recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sjd-ambulance.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Sjd-ambulance.jpg/220px-Sjd-ambulance.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Sjd-ambulance.jpg/330px-Sjd-ambulance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Sjd-ambulance.jpg/440px-Sjd-ambulance.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sjd-ambulance.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An ambulance owned by the Mexican Red Cross</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Magen_David_Adom_25th_anniversary.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1480" data-file-width="984" decoding="async" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Magen_David_Adom_25th_anniversary.jpg/220px-Magen_David_Adom_25th_anniversary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Magen_David_Adom_25th_anniversary.jpg/330px-Magen_David_Adom_25th_anniversary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Magen_David_Adom_25th_anniversary.jpg/440px-Magen_David_Adom_25th_anniversary.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Magen_David_Adom_25th_anniversary.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Israeli stamp commemorating the 25th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Magen_David_Adom" title="Magen David Adom">Magen David Adom</a>, issued 11 January 1955</div></div></div>
<p>National Red Cross and Red Crescent societies exist in nearly every country in the world. Within their home country, they take on the duties and responsibilities of a national relief society as defined by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Humanitarian_Law" title="International Humanitarian Law">International Humanitarian Law</a>. Within the Movement, the ICRC is responsible for legally recognizing a relief society as an official national Red Cross or Red Crescent society. The exact rules for recognition are defined in the statutes of the Movement. Article 4 of these statutes contains the "Conditions for recognition of National Societies":
</p>
<dl><dd><i>In order to be recognized in terms of Article 5, paragraph 2 b) as a National Society, the Society shall meet the following conditions:</i></dd></dl>
<ol><li><i>Be constituted on the territory of an independent State where the Geneva Convention for the Amelioration of the Condition of the Wounded and Sick in Armed Forces in the Field is in force.</i></li>
<li><i>Be the only National Red Cross and-or Red Crescent Society of the said State and be directed by a central body which shall alone be competent to represent it in its dealings with other components of the Movement.</i></li>
<li><i>Be duly recognized by the legal government of its country on the basis of the Geneva Conventions and of the national legislation as a voluntary aid society, auxiliary to the public authorities in the humanitarian field.</i></li>
<li><i>Have an autonomous status which allows it to operate in conformity with the Fundamental Principles of the Movement.</i></li>
<li><i>Use the name and emblem of the Red Cross or Red Crescent in conformity with the Geneva Conventions.</i></li>
<li><i>Be so organized as to be able to fulfill the tasks defined in its own statutes, including the preparation in peace time for its statutory tasks in case of armed conflict.</i></li>
<li><i>Extend its activities to the entire territory of the State.</i></li>
<li><i>Recruit its voluntary members and its staff without consideration of race, sex, class, religion or political opinions.</i></li>
<li><i>Adhere to the present Statutes, share in the fellowship which unites the components of the Movement and co-operate with them.</i></li>
<li><i>Respect the Fundamental Principles of the Movement and be guided in its work by the principles of international humanitarian law.</i></li></ol>
<p>Once a National Society has been recognized by the ICRC as a component of the International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement (the Movement), it is in principle admitted to the International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies in accordance with the terms defined in the Constitution and Rules of Procedure of the International Federation.
</p><p>Today, there are 192 National Societies recognized within the Movement and which are members of the International Federation.
</p><p>The most recent National Societies to have been recognized within the Movement are the <a href="/wiki/Maldivian_Red_Crescent" title="Maldivian Red Crescent">Maldives Red Crescent Society</a> (9 November 2011), the <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_Red_Cross" title="Cyprus Red Cross">Cyprus Red Cross Society</a>, the South Sudan Red Cross Society (12 November 2013) and, the last, the Tuvalu Red Cross Society (on 1 March 2016).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities_2">Activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Punainen_Risti_logistiikkakeskus_Kalkku_(61).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1802" data-file-width="2408" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Punainen_Risti_logistiikkakeskus_Kalkku_%2861%29.jpg/220px-Punainen_Risti_logistiikkakeskus_Kalkku_%2861%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Punainen_Risti_logistiikkakeskus_Kalkku_%2861%29.jpg/330px-Punainen_Risti_logistiikkakeskus_Kalkku_%2861%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Punainen_Risti_logistiikkakeskus_Kalkku_%2861%29.jpg/440px-Punainen_Risti_logistiikkakeskus_Kalkku_%2861%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Punainen_Risti_logistiikkakeskus_Kalkku_(61).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Logistics Centre of the <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Red_Cross" title="Finnish Red Cross">Finnish Red Cross</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tampere" title="Tampere">Tampere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a></div></div></div>
<p>Despite formal independence regarding its organizational structure and work, each national society is still bound by the laws of its home country. In many countries, national Red Cross and Red Crescent societies enjoy exceptional privileges due to agreements with their governments or specific "Red Cross Laws" granting full independence as required by the International Movement. The duties and responsibilities of a national society as defined by International Humanitarian Law and the statutes of the Movement include humanitarian aid in armed conflicts and emergency crises such as natural disasters through activities such as <a href="/wiki/Restoring_Family_Links" title="Restoring Family Links">Restoring Family Links</a>.
</p><p>Depending on their respective human, technical, financial, and organizational resources, many national societies take on additional humanitarian tasks within their home countries such as <a href="/wiki/Blood_donation" title="Blood donation">blood donation</a> services or acting as civilian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emergency_Medical_Service" title="Emergency Medical Service">Emergency Medical Service</a> (EMS) providers. The ICRC and the International Federation cooperate with the national societies in their international missions, especially with human, material, and financial resources and organizing on-site logistics.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_the_emblems">History of the emblems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: History of the emblems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Emblems_of_the_International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="Emblems of the International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">Emblems of the International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emblems_in_use">Emblems in use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Emblems in use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Red_Cross">Red Cross</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Red Cross">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="floatleft"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg"><img alt="Flag of the Red Cross.svg" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="67" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg/100px-Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg/150px-Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg/200px-Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg.png 2x" width="100"/></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Switzerland_(Pantone).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Flag_of_Switzerland_%28Pantone%29.svg/100px-Flag_of_Switzerland_%28Pantone%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Flag_of_Switzerland_%28Pantone%29.svg/150px-Flag_of_Switzerland_%28Pantone%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Flag_of_Switzerland_%28Pantone%29.svg/200px-Flag_of_Switzerland_%28Pantone%29.svg.png 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Switzerland_(Pantone).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Switzerland" title="Flag of Switzerland">flag of Switzerland</a> – basis of the original Red Cross</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>Red Cross</b> emblem was officially approved in Geneva in 1863.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Red Cross flag is not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Saint_George%27s_Cross" title="Saint George's Cross">Saint George's Cross</a> depicted on the flags of <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_England" title="Flag of England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Barcelona" title="Flag of Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Georgia_(country)" title="Flag of Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freiburg_im_Breisgau" title="Freiburg im Breisgau">Freiburg im Breisgau</a>, and several other places. In order to avoid this confusion the protected symbol is sometimes referred to as the "Greek Red Cross"; that term is also used in <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> law to describe the Red Cross. The red cross of the Saint George cross extends to the edge of the flag, whereas the red cross on the Red Cross flag does not.
</p><p>The Red Cross flag is the colour-switched version of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Switzerland" title="Flag of Switzerland">Flag of Switzerland</a>, in recognition of "the pioneering work of Swiss citizens in establishing internationally recognized standards for the protection of wounded combatants and military medical facilities."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmsf_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-jmsf-31">[30]</a></sup> In 1906, to put an end to the argument of the Ottoman Empire that the flag took its roots from Christianity, it was decided officially to promote the idea that the Red Cross flag had been formed by reversing the federal colours of <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, although no written evidence of this origin had ever been found.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoissier198577_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoissier198577-32">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1899 convention signed at the Hague extended the use of the Red Cross flag to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_ensigns" title="Naval ensigns">naval ensigns</a>, requiring that "all hospital ships shall make themselves known by hoisting, together with their national flag, the white flag with a red cross provided by the Geneva Convention."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jmsf_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-jmsf-31">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Red_Crescent">Red Crescent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Red Crescent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="floatleft"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Red_Crescent.svg"><img alt="Flag of the Red Crescent.svg" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="67" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_the_Red_Crescent.svg/100px-Flag_of_the_Red_Crescent.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_the_Red_Crescent.svg/150px-Flag_of_the_Red_Crescent.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_the_Red_Crescent.svg/200px-Flag_of_the_Red_Crescent.svg.png 2x" width="100"/></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_(1844%E2%80%931922).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="67" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Flag_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_%281844%E2%80%931922%29.svg/100px-Flag_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_%281844%E2%80%931922%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Flag_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_%281844%E2%80%931922%29.svg/150px-Flag_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_%281844%E2%80%931922%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Flag_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_%281844%E2%80%931922%29.svg/200px-Flag_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_%281844%E2%80%931922%29.svg.png 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Ottoman_Empire_(1844%E2%80%931922).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>) – basis of original Red Crescent</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>Red Crescent</b> emblem was first used by ICRC volunteers during the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)">armed conflict of 1876–1878</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>. The symbol was officially adopted in 1929, and so far 33 states in the Muslim world have recognized it. In common with the official promotion of the red cross symbol as a colour-reversal of the Swiss flag (rather than a religious symbol), the red crescent is similarly presented as being derived from a colour-reversal of the flag of the Ottoman Empire.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Red_Crystal">Red Crystal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Red Crystal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="floatleft"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Red_Crystal.svg"><img alt="Flag of the Red Crystal.svg" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="67" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Flag_of_the_Red_Crystal.svg/100px-Flag_of_the_Red_Crystal.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Flag_of_the_Red_Crystal.svg/150px-Flag_of_the_Red_Crystal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Flag_of_the_Red_Crystal.svg/200px-Flag_of_the_Red_Crystal.svg.png 2x" width="100"/></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Red_Crystal_with_Star.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Red_Crystal_with_Star.svg/100px-Red_Crystal_with_Star.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Red_Crystal_with_Star.svg/150px-Red_Crystal_with_Star.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Red_Crystal_with_Star.svg/200px-Red_Crystal_with_Star.svg.png 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Red_Crystal_with_Star.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>International emblem for <a href="/wiki/Magen_David_Adom" title="Magen David Adom">Magen David Adom</a> outside <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The International Committee of the Red Cross (ICRC) was concerned with the possibility that the two previous symbols (Red Cross and Red Crescent) were conveying religious meanings which would not be compatible with, for example, a majority <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a> or <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> country from the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific" title="Asia-Pacific">Asia-Pacific</a> region, where the majority did not associate with these symbols. Therefore, in 1992, the then-president <a href="/wiki/Cornelio_Sommaruga" title="Cornelio Sommaruga">Cornelio Sommaruga</a> decided that a third, more neutral symbol was required.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>On 8 December 2005, in response to growing pressure to accommodate <a href="/wiki/Magen_David_Adom" title="Magen David Adom">Magen David Adom</a> (MDA), Israel's national emergency medical, disaster, ambulance, and blood bank service, as a full member of the Red Cross and Red Crescent movement, a new emblem (officially the <b>Third Protocol Emblem</b>, but more commonly known as the <b>Red Crystal</b>) was adopted by an amendment of the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Conventions" title="Geneva Conventions">Geneva Conventions</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Protocol_III" title="Protocol III">Protocol III</a>, thereby fulfilling Sommaruga's call.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The Crystal can be found on official buildings and occasionally in the field. This symbolises equality and has no political, religious, or geographical connotations, thus allowing any country not comfortable with the symbolism of the original two flags to join the movement.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognised_emblems_in_disuse">Recognised emblems in disuse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Recognised emblems in disuse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Red_Lion_and_Sun">Red Lion and Sun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Red Lion and Sun">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="floatleft"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Red_Lion_with_Sun.svg"><img alt="Red Lion with Sun.svg" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="67" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Red_Lion_with_Sun.svg/100px-Red_Lion_with_Sun.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Red_Lion_with_Sun.svg/150px-Red_Lion_with_Sun.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Red_Lion_with_Sun.svg/200px-Red_Lion_with_Sun.svg.png 2x" width="100"/></a></div>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/Red_Lion_and_Sun_Society" title="Red Lion and Sun Society">Red Lion and Sun Society</a> of Iran</b> was established in 1922 and admitted to the Red Cross and Red Crescent movement in 1923.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> The symbol was introduced at Geneva in 1864,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> as a counter example to the crescent and cross used by two of Iran's rivals, the Ottoman and the Russian empires. Although that claim is inconsistent with the Red Crescent's history, that history also suggests that the Red Lion and Sun, like the Red Crescent, may have been conceived during the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)">1877–1878 war between Russia and Turkey</a>.
</p><p>Due to the emblem's association with the Iranian monarchy, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_Republic_of_Iran" title="Islamic Republic of Iran">Islamic Republic of Iran</a> replaced the Red Lion and Sun with the Red Crescent in 1980, consistent with two existing Red Cross and Red Crescent symbols. Although the Red Lion and Sun has now fallen into disuse, Iran has in the past reserved the right to take it up again at any time; the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Conventions" title="Geneva Conventions">Geneva Conventions</a> continue to recognize it as an official emblem, and that status was confirmed by <a href="/wiki/Protocol_III" title="Protocol III">Protocol III</a> in 2005 even as it added the Red Crystal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unrecognised_emblems">Unrecognised emblems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Unrecognised emblems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Red_Star_of_David">Red Star of David</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Red Star of David">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Magen_David_Adom" title="Magen David Adom">Magen David Adom</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_MAGEN_DAVID_ADOM_WORKER_IN_THE_TEL_AVIV_CIVIL_DEFENSE._%D7%9E%D7%AA%D7%A0%D7%93%D7%91%D7%AA_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%9E%D7%92%D7%9F_%D7%93%D7%95%D7%93_%D7%90%D7%93%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%A8_%D7%94%D7%90%D7%96%D7%A8%D7%97%D7%99.D23-016.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/A_MAGEN_DAVID_ADOM_WORKER_IN_THE_TEL_AVIV_CIVIL_DEFENSE._%D7%9E%D7%AA%D7%A0%D7%93%D7%91%D7%AA_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%9E%D7%92%D7%9F_%D7%93%D7%95%D7%93_%D7%90%D7%93%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%A8_%D7%94%D7%90%D7%96%D7%A8%D7%97%D7%99.D23-016.jpg/140px-A_MAGEN_DAVID_ADOM_WORKER_IN_THE_TEL_AVIV_CIVIL_DEFENSE._%D7%9E%D7%AA%D7%A0%D7%93%D7%91%D7%AA_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%9E%D7%92%D7%9F_%D7%93%D7%95%D7%93_%D7%90%D7%93%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%A8_%D7%94%D7%90%D7%96%D7%A8%D7%97%D7%99.D23-016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/A_MAGEN_DAVID_ADOM_WORKER_IN_THE_TEL_AVIV_CIVIL_DEFENSE._%D7%9E%D7%AA%D7%A0%D7%93%D7%91%D7%AA_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%9E%D7%92%D7%9F_%D7%93%D7%95%D7%93_%D7%90%D7%93%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%A8_%D7%94%D7%90%D7%96%D7%A8%D7%97%D7%99.D23-016.jpg/210px-A_MAGEN_DAVID_ADOM_WORKER_IN_THE_TEL_AVIV_CIVIL_DEFENSE._%D7%9E%D7%AA%D7%A0%D7%93%D7%91%D7%AA_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%9E%D7%92%D7%9F_%D7%93%D7%95%D7%93_%D7%90%D7%93%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%A8_%D7%94%D7%90%D7%96%D7%A8%D7%97%D7%99.D23-016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/A_MAGEN_DAVID_ADOM_WORKER_IN_THE_TEL_AVIV_CIVIL_DEFENSE._%D7%9E%D7%AA%D7%A0%D7%93%D7%91%D7%AA_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%9E%D7%92%D7%9F_%D7%93%D7%95%D7%93_%D7%90%D7%93%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%A8_%D7%94%D7%90%D7%96%D7%A8%D7%97%D7%99.D23-016.jpg/280px-A_MAGEN_DAVID_ADOM_WORKER_IN_THE_TEL_AVIV_CIVIL_DEFENSE._%D7%9E%D7%AA%D7%A0%D7%93%D7%91%D7%AA_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%9E%D7%92%D7%9F_%D7%93%D7%95%D7%93_%D7%90%D7%93%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%A8_%D7%94%D7%90%D7%96%D7%A8%D7%97%D7%99.D23-016.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_MAGEN_DAVID_ADOM_WORKER_IN_THE_TEL_AVIV_CIVIL_DEFENSE._%D7%9E%D7%AA%D7%A0%D7%93%D7%91%D7%AA_%D7%A9%D7%9C_%D7%9E%D7%92%D7%9F_%D7%93%D7%95%D7%93_%D7%90%D7%93%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%91%D7%9E%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%A8_%D7%94%D7%90%D7%96%D7%A8%D7%97%D7%99.D23-016.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Magen_David_Adom" title="Magen David Adom">Magen David Adom</a> worker in the <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> civil defense, 1939</div></div></div>
<div class="floatleft"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Red_Star_of_David.svg"><img alt="Red Star of David.svg" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="67" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Red_Star_of_David.svg/100px-Red_Star_of_David.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Red_Star_of_David.svg/150px-Red_Star_of_David.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Red_Star_of_David.svg/200px-Red_Star_of_David.svg.png 2x" width="100"/></a></div>
<p>For over 50 years, Israel requested the addition of a red <a href="/wiki/Star_of_David" title="Star of David">Star of David</a>, arguing that since Christian and Muslim emblems were recognized, the corresponding Jewish emblem should be as well. This emblem has been used by <a href="/wiki/Magen_David_Adom" title="Magen David Adom">Magen David Adom</a> (MDA), or Red Star of David, but it is not recognized by the Geneva Conventions as a protected symbol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> The first use of the "Magen David Adom" was during the Anglo Boer War in South Africa (1899–1902) when it was used by the Ambulance Corps founded by Ben Zion Aaron in Johannesburg as a first aid corps to assist the Boer forces. Permission was given by President Paul Kruger of the South African Republic for the Star of David to be used as its insignia, rather than the conventional red cross.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Saxe1929105–110_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Saxe1929105–110-37">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Red Star of David is not recognized as a protected symbol outside Israel; instead the MDA uses the Red Crystal emblem during international operations in order to ensure protection. Depending on the circumstances, it may place the Red Star of David inside the Red Crystal, or use the Red Crystal alone.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hostage_crisis_allegations">Hostage crisis allegations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Hostage crisis allegations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Australian TV network <a href="/wiki/ABC_Television_(Australian_TV_network)" title="ABC Television (Australian TV network)">ABC</a> and the indigenous rights group <a href="/wiki/Rettet_die_Naturv%C3%B6lker" title="Rettet die Naturvölker">Rettet die Naturvölker</a> released a documentary called <i>Blood on the Cross</i> in 1999. It alleged the involvement of the Red Cross with the British and Indonesian military in a massacre in the Southern Highlands of <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Western New Guinea</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mapenduma_hostage_crisis" title="Mapenduma hostage crisis">Mapenduma hostage crisis</a> of May 1996, when Western and Indonesian activists were held hostage by separatists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fpcnvideos_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-fpcnvideos-38">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeith2002305–6_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeith2002305–6-39">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the broadcast of the documentary, the Red Cross announced publicly that it would appoint an individual outside the organization to investigate the allegations made in the film and any responsibility on its part. Piotr Obuchowicz was appointed to investigate the matter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> The report categorically states that the Red Cross personnel accused of involvement were proven not to have been present; that a white helicopter was probably used in a military operation, but the helicopter was not a Red Cross helicopter, and must have been painted by one of several military organizations operating in the region at the time. Perhaps the Red Cross logo itself was also used, although no hard evidence was found for this; that this was part of the military operation to free the hostages, but was clearly intended to achieve surprise by deceiving the local people into thinking that a Red Cross helicopter was landing; and that the Red Cross should have responded more quickly and thoroughly to investigate the allegations than it did.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Explanatory_notes">Explanatory notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Explanatory notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Livia_Rothkirchen" title="Livia Rothkirchen">Livia Rothkirchen</a>: "In contrast to those of the Danish delegates, Rossel's report was phrased in positive terms,  falling in line with German propaganda."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERothkirchen2006258_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERothkirchen2006258-17">[17]</a></sup></li><li><a href="/wiki/Lucy_Dawidowicz" title="Lucy Dawidowicz">Lucy Dawidowicz</a>: "[Rossel's] acceptance of everything he had seen... and everything he had been told... was total and complacent. The report which he prepared for his superiors in the Red Cross was exactly what the Germans had hoped for... a totally uncritical, even approving affirmation of their propaganda."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDawidowicz1975138_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDawidowicz1975138-18">[18]</a></sup></li></ul></div></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation news cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://www.irinnews.org/news/2003/03/28/swiss-icrc-delegate-murdered" rel="nofollow">"Swiss ICRC delegate murdered"</a>. <i>www.irinnews.org</i>. <a href="/wiki/The_New_Humanitarian" title="The New Humanitarian">The New Humanitarian</a>. 28 March 2003<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">8 March</span> 2016</span>. <q>Ricardo Munguia, a Swiss citizen of Salvadorian origin was travelling with Afghan colleagues on an assignment to improve the water supply to the district. He was shot in cold blood on Thursday by a group of unidentified assailants who stopped the vehicles transporting them ... the assailants had shot the 39-year-old water and habitat engineer in the head and burned one car, warning two Afghans accompanying him not to work for foreigners ... Asked what action ICRC was taking, Bouvier explained that for the time being, the ICRC has decided to temporarily freeze all field trips in Afghanistan, calling all staff to the main delegation's offices.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=www.irinnews.org&amp;rft.atitle=Swiss+ICRC+delegate+murdered&amp;rft.date=2003-03-28&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.irinnews.org%2Fnews%2F2003%2F03%2F28%2Fswiss-icrc-delegate-murdered&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AInternational+Red+Cross+and+Red+Crescent+Movement"></span></span>
